    1. 1
      Installing The Framework [0 ms]

      Scenarios 1 0 0 
      As a developer
You can leverage xBDD within your .Net testing projects
By installing the xBDD.Core nuget package

      1. 3 Via A Nuget Package [0 ms]

        1. Given you have created a test project [0 ms]
        2. When you excute the following command in the project directory: [Input] [0 ms] 
          dotnet add package xBDD
        3. Then you will install the xBDD framework [0 ms]

    2. 2
      Executing Your First Scenario [60,040 ms]

      Scenarios 2 0 0 
      As a developer
You can automate a basic scenario
By using xB.AddScenario and the Given, When, Then, and And operations.

      1. 3 Executing A Passing Web UI Scenario In An MS Test Project [29,066 ms]

        1. Given you have a similar class in your test project for defining a passing scenario: [Output] [2 ms] 
          namespace Amazon.Features.SearchingProducts
{
    using Microsoft.VisualStudio.TestTools.UnitTesting;
    using System;
    using System.Threading.Tasks;
    using xBDD;
    using xBDD.Browser;

	[TestClass]
	[AsA("anonymous user")]
	[YouCan("search across all amazon products")]
	[By("using primary search bar on the home page")]
	public class SearchingAllProducts: IFeature
	{
		private User you = new User();
		public IOutputWriter OutputWriter { get; private set; }

		public SearchingAllProducts()
		{
			OutputWriter = new TestContextWriter();
		}
		
		[TestMethod]
		public async Task SearchWithSearchButton()
		{
			await xB.AddScenario(this)
				.Given(you.NavigateTo("the amazon home page","https://www.amazon.com"))
				.When(you.EnterTheText("echo").In("the search box", "#twotabsearchtextbox"))
				.And(you.Click("the search button", "input[type=submit]"))
				.Then(you.WillSee("the search results section", "#s-results-list-atf").IsVisible())
				.Run();
		}
	}
}
        2. When you run the MS Test Project with the following command: [Input] [Output] [29,032 ms] 
          dotnet test -v n --filter FullyQualifiedName=Amazon.Features.SearchingProducts.SearchingAllProducts.SearchWithSearchButton

    3. 1
      Skipping A Scenario [8,509 ms]

      Scenarios 1 0 0 
      As a developer
You can include (document) scenarios that are not ready to run
By calling the Skip method on the scenario instead of the Run method.

      1. 3 Running A Skipped Scenario [8,509 ms]

        1. Given you have a similar class in your test project that defines a skipped scenario: [Output] [0 ms] 
          namespace Amazon.Features.SearchingProducts
{
    using Microsoft.VisualStudio.TestTools.UnitTesting;
    using System;
    using System.Threading.Tasks;
    using xBDD;
    using xBDD.Browser;

	[TestClass]
	[AsA("anonymous user")]
	[YouCan("search across all amazon products")]
	[By("using primary search bar on the home page")]
	public class SearchingAllProducts_Skipped: IFeature
	{
		private User you = new User();
		public IOutputWriter OutputWriter { get; private set; }

		public SearchingAllProducts_Skipped()
		{
			OutputWriter = new TestContextWriter();
		}
		
		[TestMethod]
		public async Task SearchWithSearchButton_Skipped()
		{
			await xB.AddScenario(this)
				.Given(you.NavigateTo("the amazon home page","https://www.amazon.com"))
				.When(you.EnterTheText("echo").In("the search box", "#twotabsearchtextbox"))
				.And(you.Click("the search button", "input[type=submit]"))
				.Then(you.WillSee("the search results section", "#BAD_SELECTOR").IsVisible())
				.Skip("Not implemented", Assert.Inconclusive);
		}
	}
}

    4. 1
      Using A Scenario To Create Documentation [8,181 ms]

      Scenarios 1 0 0 
      As a developer
You can add a scenario that only creates documentation and does not run any code
By calling the Document method on the scenario

      1. 3 Running A Documentation Scenario [8,181 ms]

        1. Given you have a similar class in your test project that executes a documentation scenario: [Output] [0 ms] 
          namespace Amazon.Features.SearchingProducts
{
    using Microsoft.VisualStudio.TestTools.UnitTesting;
    using System;
    using System.Threading.Tasks;
    using xBDD;
    using xBDD.Browser;

	[TestClass]
	[AsA("developer")]
	[YouCan("verify that your code changes did not cause a regression")]
	[By("using the continuous integration pipeline")]
	public class ContinuousIntegration: IFeature
	{
		private User you = new User();
		public IOutputWriter OutputWriter { get; private set; }

		public ContinuousIntegration()
		{
			OutputWriter = new TestContextWriter();
		}
		
		[TestMethod]
		public async Task PassingCheckIn()
		{
			await xB.AddScenario(this)
				.Given("you have made a code change")
				.When("you check in the change")
				.Then("the build server will build and run all tests")
				.Document();
		}
	}
}

    5. 1
      Leveraging Reusable Steps [55 ms]

      Scenarios 1 0 0 
      As a developer
You can simplify the development of tests
By using a library of reusable steps

      1. 4 By Inheriting From The User Class [55 ms]

        1. Given you have a similar class in your test project for defining reusable steps: [Output] [0 ms] 
          namespace Amazon.Features.Actors
{
	using Microsoft.VisualStudio.TestTools.UnitTesting;
	using System;
	using System.Threading.Tasks;
	using xBDD;
	using xBDD.Model;
	using xBDD.Browser;

	public class AnonymousUser: User
	{
		public const string Name = "anonymous user";
		public Step NavigateToTheHomePage()
		{
			return xB.CreateAsyncStep(
				"you navigate to the home page", 
				async step => {
					await Task.Run(() => {
						// some async action...
					});
				}
			);
		}

		public Step EnterTheSearchText(string text)
		{
			return xB.CreateStep(
				$"you enter the search text '{text}'", 
				step => {/* some action... */ }
			);
		}
		public Step ClickTheSearchButton()
		{
			return xB.CreateStep(
				$"you click the search button", 
				step => {/* some action... */ }
			);
		}
		public Step WillSeeTheSearchResults()
		{
			return xB.CreateStep(
				$"you will see the search results", 
				step => {/* some action... */ }
			);
		}
		public Step SubmitTheSearchWithTheEnterKey()
		{
			return xB.CreateStep(
				$"you submit the search by pressing the enter key", 
				step => {/* some action... */ }
			);
		}
	}
}
        2. And you have a similar class in your test project that defines a feature using the reusable steps: [Output] [0 ms] 
          namespace Amazon.Features.SearchingProducts
{
	using Microsoft.VisualStudio.TestTools.UnitTesting;
	using System;
	using System.Threading.Tasks;
	using xBDD;
	using xBDD.Model;
	using xBDD.Browser;
	using Amazon.Features.Actors;

	[TestClass]
	[AsA(AnonymousUser.Name)]
	[YouCan("search across all amazon products")]
	[By("using the primary search bar on the home page")]
	public class SearchingAllProducts_ReusableSteps: IFeature
	{
		private AnonymousUser you = new AnonymousUser();
		public IOutputWriter OutputWriter { get; private set; }

		public SearchingAllProducts_ReusableSteps()
		{
			OutputWriter = new TestContextWriter();
		}
		
		[TestMethod]
		public async Task SearchWithSearchButton_ReusableSteps()
		{
			await xB.AddScenario(this)
				.Given(you.NavigateToTheHomePage())
				.When(you.EnterTheSearchText("echo"))
				.And(you.ClickTheSearchButton())
				.Then(you.WillSeeTheSearchResults())
				.Run();
		}
		[TestMethod]
		public async Task SearchWithEnter_ReusableSteps()
		{
			await xB.AddScenario(this)
				.Given(you.NavigateToTheHomePage())
				.When(you.EnterTheSearchText("echo"))
				.And(you.SubmitTheSearchWithTheEnterKey())
				.Then(you.WillSeeTheSearchResults())
				.Run();
		}
	}
}

        5. And you will see the feature 1 with yellow badge is visible [41 ms]
        6. And you will see the feature 1 scenarios is not visible because none were failing [25 ms]

      3. 5 Failing [299 ms]

        1. Given you generate an html report from test results of a single failed scenario [2 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single failed scenario [138 ms]
        3. And you click when the area title line is visible [96 ms]
        4. Then you will see the feature 1 with red badge is visible [33 ms]
        5. And you will see the feature 1 scenarios is not visible because the Failures Only option was not set to true that would cause the failred feature to automatically expand. [27 ms]

    9. 4
      Review Feature Scenario Distribution [1,678 ms]

      Scenarios 4 0 0 
      As a Developer
You can see the distribution of feature outcomes for an area
By reviewing the distribution graph next to the area badge

      1. 9 Failed Skipped And Passing Scenario Stats [459 ms]

        1. Given you generate an html report from test results of a full test run with all outcomes [10 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a full test run with all outcomes [75 ms]
        3. And you click when the area title line is visible [98 ms]
        4. Then you will see feature badge and distribution chart is visible [49 ms]
        5. And you will see feature badge and distribution chart has a title attribute of Scenarios [31 ms]
        6. And you will see feature scenario distribution chart is visible [31 ms]
        7. And you will see feature scenario distribution passed bar has a heigth of 33% [44 ms]
        8. And you will see feature scenario distribution skipped bar has a heigth of 33% [48 ms]
        9. And you will see feature scenario distribution failed bar has a heigth of 33% [69 ms]

      2. 8 All Passing Scenario Stats [550 ms]

        1. Given you generate an html report from test results of a passing full test run [8 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a passing full test run [104 ms]
        3. And you wait till the area title line is visible [32 ms]
        4. And you click when the area title line is visible [218 ms]
        5. Then you will see feature scenario distribution chart is visible [63 ms]
        6. And you will see feature scenario distribution passed bar has a heigth of 100% [74 ms]
        7. And you will see feature scenario distribution skipped bar is not there [23 ms]
        8. And you will see feature scenario distribution failed bar is not there [24 ms]

      3. 8 All Skipped Scenario Stats [378 ms]

        1. Given you generate an html report from test results of a single skipped scenario [1 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single skipped scenario [141 ms]
        3. And you wait till the area title line is visible [32 ms]
        4. And you click when the area title line is visible [111 ms]

        6. And you will see feature scenario distribution skipped bar has a heigth of 100% [42 ms]

        8. And you will see feature scenario distribution failed bar is not there [8 ms]

You can understand more detail about a feature

      1. 4 Collapsed By Default [313 ms]

      3. 6 Partially Sorted [488 ms]

        1. Given you generate an html report from a test run that is sorted [5 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the sample test html report that is sorted [119 ms]
        3. And you click when the area title line is visible [103 ms]
        4. And you click when the feature name is visible [114 ms]
        5. Then you will see the feature name has text 'Sample Skipped Feature' because it was the second in the feature sort [Output] [71 ms]

      12. 3 Write Run Scenario With Step With Multiline Parameter [4 ms]

        1. Given you have a similar class in your test project : [Output] [0 ms] 
          using System.Threading.Tasks;
using xBDD.Features;
namespace xBDD.Features.GenerateReports.GenerateTextReport.WriteToTextScenarios
{
    public class RunScenarioWithStepWithMultilineParameter : IExecute<string>
    {
        public async Task<string> Execute()
        {
            var xBDD = new xBDDMock();
            xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.Name = "My Test Run";
            await xBDD.CurrentRun
                .AddScenario("My Scenario", "My Feature", "My.Area.Path")
                .Given(xBDD.CreateStep("my starting condition with the following", (s) => { }, $"My{System.Environment.NewLine}multiline{System.Environment.NewLine}parameter"))
                .When(xBDD.CreateStep("my action"))
                .Then(xBDD.CreateStep("my ending condition"))
                .Run();
            return await xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.WriteToText();
        }
    }
